Viacheslav: Short answer: STVARUINT16 is about the length field of a variable‚Äëlength integer, not the width of the stored value. The opcode name doesn‚Äôt mean ‚Äústore a 16‚Äëbit integer‚Äù ‚Äî it means ‚Äústore a VarUInteger whose length prefix is 16 bits‚Äù.

Antoxa: –Ø –ø–æ—Ö–æ–¥—É –ø–æ–Ω—è–ª –≤ —á–µ–º –ø—Ä–æ–±–ª–µ–º–∞, –∫–æ–≥–¥–∞ –∏–¥–µ—Ç –ø—Ä–æ–≤–µ—Ä–∫–∞, –∫–æ—à–µ–ª–µ–∫ –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç, –∞ –Ω–æ–º–µ—Ä —Ç—Ä–∞–Ω–∑–∞–∫—Ü–∏–∏ –Ω–µ—Ç, —Ç–∞–∫ –∫–∞–∫ –ø—Ä–∏ –æ–ø–ª–∞—Ç–µ –æ–Ω –≤–æ–∑–≤—Ä–∞—â–∞–µ—Ç—Å—è –≤ –¥—Ä—É–≥–æ–º —Ñ–æ—Ä–º–∞—Ç–µ –∫–∞–∫ —è –ø–æ–Ω—è–ª –∏ –º–Ω–µ –∫–∞–∫-—Ç–æ –≤–∏–¥–∏–º–æ –∫–æ–Ω–≤–µ—Ä—Ç–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å –µ–≥–æ –Ω–∞–¥–æ ! —á—Ç–æ–±—ã –µ–≥–æ –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥–∏–ª–æ.  /**    * –ü—Ä–µ–æ–±—Ä–∞–∑—É–µ—Ç Raw-–∞–¥—Ä–µ—Å ("0:hex") –≤ User-friendly —Ñ–æ—Ä–º–∞—Ç ("EQ...").    * –≠—Ç–∞ –≤–µ—Ä—Å–∏—è –∫–æ—Ä—Ä–µ–∫—Ç–Ω–æ —Ä–∞–±–æ—Ç–∞–µ—Ç —Å —Å–æ–≤—Ä–µ–º–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–º–∏ –∫–æ—à–µ–ª—å–∫–∞–º–∏ (v3, v4)    * –∏ –∏—Å–ø–æ–ª—å–∑—É–µ—Ç –Ω–∞–¥–µ–∂–Ω—ã–π –º–µ—Ç–æ–¥ —É–ø–∞–∫–æ–≤–∫–∏ –±–∞–π—Ç–æ–≤.    */   private function rawToUserFriendly ($rawAddress)     {     // –†–∞–∑–±–∏—Ä–∞–µ–º –∞–¥—Ä–µ—Å –Ω–∞ workchain –∏ hash     list($workchain, $hash) = explode (':', $rawAddress);     $workchain = (int) $workchain;     $hashBytes = hex2bin ($hash);      // –§–æ—Ä–º–∏—Ä—É–µ–º –æ—Å–Ω–æ–≤–Ω–æ–π –±–∞–π—Ç–æ–≤—ã–π –º–∞—Å—Å–∏–≤     // –¢–µ–≥ –¥–ª—è bounceable –∞–¥—Ä–µ—Å–∞: 0x11     $tag = 0x11;      $addressBytes = pack ('c', $tag) . pack ('c', $workchain) . $hashBytes;      // –°—á–∏—Ç–∞–µ–º –∫–æ–Ω—Ç—Ä–æ–ª—å–Ω—É—é —Å—É–º–º—É     $crc = $this->crc16 ($addressBytes);      // –î–æ–±–∞–≤–ª—è–µ–º –∫–æ–Ω—Ç—Ä–æ–ª—å–Ω—É—é —Å—É–º–º—É –≤ –∫–æ–Ω–µ—Ü     // –ò–°–ü–†–ê–í–õ–ï–ù–ò–ï: –ò—Å–ø–æ–ª—å–∑—É–µ–º 'v' –¥–ª—è little-endian —É–ø–∞–∫–æ–≤–∫–∏.     // –≠—Ç–æ –±–æ–ª–µ–µ –Ω–∞–¥–µ–∂–Ω—ã–π —Å–ø–æ—Å–æ–±.     $fullAddressBytes = $addressBytes . pack ('v', $crc);      // –ö–æ–¥–∏—Ä—É–µ–º –≤ base64url     return rtrim (strtr (base64_encode ($fullAddressBytes), '+/', '-_'), '=');     }   /**    * –í—ã—á–∏—Å–ª—è–µ—Ç CRC16-CCITT-FALSE, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–π –∏—Å–ø–æ–ª—å–∑—É–µ—Ç—Å—è –≤ TON.    * –≠—Ç–∞ —Ñ—É–Ω–∫—Ü–∏—è —è–≤–ª—è–µ—Ç—Å—è –≤—Å–ø–æ–º–æ–≥–∞—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–æ–π –¥–ª—è rawToUserFriendly.    */   private function crc16 ($data)     {     $crc = 0xFFFF;     for ($i = 0; $i < strlen ($data); $i++)       {       $crc ^= ord ($data[$i]) << 8;       for ($j = 0; $j < 8; $j++)         {         $crc = ($crc & 0x8000) ? ($crc << 1) ^ 0x1021 : $crc << 1;         }       }     return $crc & 0xFFFF;     } –ü–æ—Ö–æ–¥—É –ø—Ä–∏—á–∏–Ω–∞ –∏–∑-–∑–∞ —Ç–æ–≥–æ, —á—Ç–æ —è —Å–∞–º —Å–µ–±–µ –æ–ø–ª–∞—Ç—É –¥–µ–ª–∞–ª, –∫–æ–≥–¥–∞ —Ç–µ—Å—Ç–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–ª, —â–∞—Å –ø–æ–º–µ–Ω—è–ª, –∏ –ø–æ–π–º–∞–ª (Toncenter API - 500 Internal Server Error) (reply to 324039)

üêº Sild: –ê –≤ –¥–∏–∫—Ç–µ (HashMap) –∫–ª—é—á –º–æ–∂–µ—Ç –±—ã—Ç—å –¥–ª–∏–Ω–Ω–µ–µ 256 –±–∏—Ç?

&rey: –ú–æ–∂–µ—Ç. –í –ø—Ä–∏–Ω—Ü–∏–ø–µ, –¥–∞–∂–µ 900 –º–æ–∂–Ω–æ –≤–º–µ—Å—Ç–∏—Ç—å. (reply to 324094)

üêº Sild: –º–Ω–æ–≥–æ –¥–æ—á–µ—Ä–Ω–∏—Ö —Å–µ–ª–æ–≤ —Ç–∞–º –∏–∑-–∑–∞ —Ç–æ–≥–æ —á—Ç–æ –ø—Ä–µ—Ñ–∏–∫—Å–Ω–æ–µ –¥–µ—Ä–µ–≤–æ —á–∞—Å—Ç–æ –¥–µ–ª–∏—Ç—Å—è

–õ: async def send_ton(to_addr: str, amount_ton: float) -> bool:     wallet_addr = wallet.address.to_string(False, False, False)     amount_nanoton = int(round(amount_ton * 1e9))      async with httpx.AsyncClient(timeout=15) as client:         resp = await client.get(f"https://toncenter.com/api/v2/getWalletInformation", params={"address": wallet_addr})         if resp.status_code != 200:             print(f"–û—à–∏–±–∫–∞ –ø–æ–ª—É—á–µ–Ω–∏—è seqno: {resp.text}")             return False         data = resp.json()         if not data.get("ok") or "result" not in data:             print(f"–ù–µ–≤–µ—Ä–Ω—ã–π –æ—Ç–≤–µ—Ç –ø—Ä–∏ –ø–æ–ª—É—á–µ–Ω–∏–∏ seqno: {data}")             return False         seqno = data["result"]["seqno"]          try:             msg = wallet.create_transfer_message(                 to_addr=to_addr,                 amount=amount_nanoton,                 seqno=seqno,                 send_mode=3             )         except Exception as e:             print(f"–û—à–∏–±–∫–∞ —Å–æ–∑–¥–∞–Ω–∏—è —Ç—Ä–∞–Ω–∑–∞–∫—Ü–∏–∏: {e}")             return False                  boc_b64 = base64.b64encode(msg["message"].to_boc()).decode()                   send_resp = await client.post(f"https://toncenter.com/api/v2/sendBoc", json={"boc": boc_b64})         if send_resp.status_code == 200:             resp_data = send_resp.json()             if resp_data.get("ok"):                 return True             else:                 print(f"–û—à–∏–±–∫–∞ –æ—Ç–ø—Ä–∞–≤–∫–∏ BOC: {resp_data}")         else:             print(f"HTTP –æ—à–∏–±–∫–∞ –ø—Ä–∏ –æ—Ç–ø—Ä–∞–≤–∫–µ BOC: {send_resp.status_code} {send_resp.text}")      return False   —á–µ –Ω–µ —Ç–∞–∫, —Ö—ç–ª–ø, –æ—Å–æ–±–æ –Ω–µ —à–∞—Ä—é, –Ω–∞–¥–æ –æ–¥–Ω—É —Ñ—É–Ω–∫—Ü–∏—é —Å–¥–µ–ª–∞—Ç—å

User: üöÄ First beta release of the new TON documentation is now live! üó∫ Jump ahead to beta-docs.ton.org or stay here to learn about the project's backstory, current achievements, and future plans.  For quite some time, developers shared the same feedback: TON documentation is too scattered, difficult to navigate, and has obvious gaps and inconsistencies.  We at TON Studio took that seriously and initiated the TON Docs Revamp project in late July. It is focused on the following four goals:  ‚Ä¢ To introduce a streamlined, discoverable structure that would be easy to navigate and search ‚Ä¢ To make documentation welcoming to all developers, from newcomers to seasoned professionals ‚Ä¢ To introduce and maintain stricter quality checks from humans and AIs to ensure proof-read, up-to-date, consistent, and clear content ‚Ä¢ And, finally, to set up documentation release pipelines for major TON builders, while making community contributions straightforward and approachable  üèÜ Today, with the help and suggestions from various developer teams, including Zengo, RSquad, TonTech, TON API team, and TON Core, the TON Studio is proud to present the first public version of this documentation. It already fulfills the first goal of comprehensive structure and rapidly moves towards achieving the third goal of content.  ü¶Ñ That said, this is a beta release: many pages await their contents, some pages require secondary reviews, while infrastructure, pipelines, and processes are only nourishing, not mature yet. All constructive feedback is appreciated.  So, what's in store already? We've got:  ‚Ä¢ Flat, easy-to-navigate structure ‚Ä¢ Hands-on articles with real examples whenever we can provide them ‚Ä¢ Visuals and diagrams, including various Mermaid diagrams ‚Ä¢ Smart AI search and summaries ‚Ä¢ Automatic CI spell checks and AI reviews based on the growing style guide ‚Ä¢ ...and much, much more!  üè† TON Docs Revamp features an engaging landing page that guides users through their TON journey, whether they're first exploring TON, building smart contracts, integrating wallets, or just want to access and navigate the documentation quickly.  üìù Re-written or brand new content includes pages for: mytonctrl, mylocalton, development setups with Sandbox and Blueprint (with major help from TonTech), IDEs and SDKs, gas estimation, analytics, oracles, bridges, TMAs, TON Connect, standard wallet contracts, Jettons, NFTs, TVM instructions (with proper search and discovery), TL-B, FunC and other TON-specific programming languages, web versions of whitepapers (with cross-links and solid AI summaries), and even a "Coming from Ethereum" guide!  üìà And this is just the beginning. Plans ahead and for the next month include:  - Release pipelines and assignments of relevant technical owners - Docs, infrastructure, and processes for approachable community contributions - More playgrounds, interactive components, and interactivity - Much more content - Stronger AI-based assistance as documentation grows  üéØ The main goals of this beta release are to show preliminary progress, willingness to make things right, and to collect feedback from the developer community before the full release, which is tentatively scheduled for November 17th.  We are nothing without the feedback from the community. If something is missing or confusing, let us know by filing a GitHub issue. Furthermore, help review new content whenever you or someone you know is deeply familiar with the topic. TON is vast, and there is always something to know or be aware of.  Prominent ecosystem projects are invited to host, co-own, and maintain their documentation with us. Keeping things in one place will enrich the user experience and AI responses.   üí™ Let's make the best documentation for TON.
